   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of lunar features
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
     <span class="mw-redirectedfrom">
      (Redirected from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_features_on_the_Moon&amp;redirect=no" title="List of features on the Moon">
       List of features on the Moon
      </a>
      )
     </span>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <p>
       Several features cover the
       <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_the_Moon" title="Geology of the Moon">
        surface
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
        Moon
       </a>
       . These are listed below.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Valleys">
        Valleys
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_lunar_features&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Valleys">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Among many lunar features are several large
       <a href="/wiki/Valley" title="Valley">
        valleys
       </a>
       that have been given names. Most of these valleys are named after a nearby
       <a href="/wiki/Impact_crater" title="Impact crater">
        crater
       </a>
       ; see the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_craters_on_the_Moon" title="List of craters on the Moon">
        list of craters on the Moon
       </a>
       for more information.
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water_features">
        Water features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_lunar_features&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Water features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="floatright">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moon_names.svg" title="Lunar nearside with major Lakr and craters labeled">
        <img alt="Lunar nearside with major Lakr and craters labeled" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="512" height="375" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Moon_names.svg/500px-Moon_names.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Moon_names.svg/750px-Moon_names.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Moon_names.svg/1000px-Moon_names.svg.png 2x" width="500"/>
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       This is a list of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Lunar_mare" title="Lunar mare">
         maria
        </a>
       </i>
       (singular
       <i>
        mare
       </i>
       ) on the
       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
        Moon
       </a>
       . Lunar Maria are the large, dark, regions of the moon. They do not actually contain any water, however they are believed to have been formed from molten rock from the moon's mantle coming out onto the surface of the moon. It also includes the one
       <i>
        oceanus
       </i>
       and the features known by the names
       <i>
        lacus
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        palus
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        sinus
       </i>
       . The modern system of lunar nomenclature was introduced in 1651 by
       <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Riccioli" title="Giovanni Battista Riccioli">
        Riccioli
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Riccioli's map of the moon was drawn by
       <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Maria_Grimaldi" title="Francesco Maria Grimaldi">
        Francesco Maria Grimaldi
       </a>
       , who has a crater named after him.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>

      <p>
       There was also a region on the Lunar farside that was briefly misidentified as a mare and named
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mare_Desiderii" title="Mare Desiderii">
         Mare Desiderii
        </a>
       </i>
       (Sea of Dreams). It is no longer recognized. Other former maria include:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mare_Parvum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mare Parvum (page does not exist)">
         Mare Parvum
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telescop.htm_4-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-telescop.htm-4">
          [4]
         </a>
        </sup>
        ("Small Sea"), immediately to the east of
        <a href="/wiki/Inghirami_(crater)" title="Inghirami (crater)">
         Inghirami
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mare_Incognitum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mare Incognitum (page does not exist)">
         Mare Incognitum
        </a>
        ("Unknown Sea")
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mare_Novum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mare Novum (page does not exist)">
         Mare Novum
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telescop.htm_4-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-telescop.htm-4">
          [4]
         </a>
        </sup>
        ("New Sea"), northeast of
        <a href="/wiki/Plutarch_(crater)" title="Plutarch (crater)">
         Plutarch
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mare_Struve&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mare Struve (page does not exist)">
         Mare Struve
        </a>
        ("Struve's Sea"), near
        <a href="/wiki/Messala_(crater)" title="Messala (crater)">
         Messala
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sinus_and_Paludes">
        <i>

        </i>
        and
        <i>

       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>

      <p>
       Some sources also list a
       <i>
        Palus Nebularum
       </i>
       ("Marsh of Mists") at 38.0° N, 1.0° E. However the designation for this feature has not been officially recognized by the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union" title="International Astronomical Union">
        IAU
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mountains">
        Mountains
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_lunar_features&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Mountains">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       These are isolated mountains or
       <a href="/wiki/Massif" title="Massif">
        massifs
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Note that the heights listed below are not consistent across sources. In the 1960s, the US Army Mapping Service used elevation relative to 1,737,988 meters from the center of the Moon. In the 1970s, the US Defense Mapping Agency used 1,730,000 meters. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clementine_mission" title="Clementine mission">
        Clementine
       </a>
       topographic data published in the 1990s uses 1,737,400 meters.
      </p>
      <p>
       Also note that this table is not comprehensive, and does not list the highest places on the Moon. Clementine data show a range of about 18,100 meters from lowest to highest point on the Moon.
       <a href="/wiki/Selenean_summit" title="Selenean summit">
        The highest point
       </a>
       , located on the far side of the Moon, is approximately 6500 meters higher than Mons Huygens (usually listed as the tallest mountain).
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_features">
        Other features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_lunar_features&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
        Moon
       </a>
       's surface is covered in many interesting geological features. In addition to
       <a href="/wiki/Mountain" title="Mountain">
        mountains
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Valley" title="Valley">
        valleys
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Impact_crater" title="Impact crater">
        craters
       </a>
       , the following surface features have received names in the
       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_nomenclature#The_Moon" title="Planetary nomenclature">
        Lunar nomenclature
       </a>
       . Many of these features are named after a nearby crater or mountain.
      </p>
      <p>
       The listed
       <a href="/wiki/Diameter" title="Diameter">
        diameter
       </a>
       for these features is the longest dimension that contains the entire geological formation. The
       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">
        latitude
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">
        longitude
       </a>
       are in
       <a href="/wiki/Selenographic_coordinates" title="Selenographic coordinates">
        selenographic coordinates
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Albedo">
        Albedo
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_lunar_features&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Albedo">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       These features are notable for their high
       <a href="/wiki/Albedo" title="Albedo">
        albedo
       </a>
       compared to the surrounding terrain.
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Name
        </th>
        <th>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Selenographic_coordinate" title="Selenographic coordinate">
          Coordinates
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Diameter" title="Diameter">
          Diameter
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         Name Origin
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Reiner_Gamma" title="Reiner Gamma">
          Reiner Gamma
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
          <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=List_of_lunar_features&amp;params=7.5_N_59.0_W_globe:Moon">
           <span class="geo-nondefault">
            <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
             <span class="latitude">
              7°30′N
             </span>
             <span class="longitude">
              59°00′W
             </span>
            </span>
           </span>
           <span class="geo-multi-punct">
            ﻿ / ﻿
           </span>
           <span class="geo-default">
            <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
             7.5°N 59.0°W
            </span>
            <span style="display:none">
             ﻿ /
             <span class="geo">
              7.5; -59.0
             </span>
            </span>
           </span>
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td align="right">
         70.0 km
        </td>
        <td>
         After nearby crater
         <a href="/wiki/Reiner_(crater)" title="Reiner (crater)">
          Reiner
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <i>
        Note:
       </i>
       On the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Far_side_(Moon)" title="Far side (Moon)">
        far side
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
        Moon
       </a>
       there are unnamed albedo features on
       <a href="/wiki/Mare_Ingenii" title="Mare Ingenii">
        Mare Ingenii
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mare_Marginis" title="Mare Marginis">
        Mare Marginis
       </a>
       . These are located
       <a href="/wiki/Antipodes" title="Antipodes">
        antipodal
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Mare_Imbrium" title="Mare Imbrium">
        Mare Imbrium
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mare_Orientale" title="Mare Orientale">
        Mare Orientale
       </a>
       impact basins.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Catena">
        Catena
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_lunar_features&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Catena">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dorsa">
        Dorsa
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_lunar_features&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Dorsa">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       These features are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wrinkle-ridge" title="Wrinkle-ridge">
        wrinkle-ridge
       </a>
       systems commonly found on
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_mare" title="Lunar mare">
        lunar maria
       </a>
       .
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dorsum">
        Dorsum
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_lunar_features&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Dorsum">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       These features are
       <a href="/wiki/Wrinkle_ridge" title="Wrinkle ridge">
        wrinkle ridges
       </a>
       commonly found on
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_mare" title="Lunar mare">
        lunar mare
       </a>
      </p>

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Promontorium">
        Promontorium
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_lunar_features&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Promontorium">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       These features form a
       <a href="/wiki/Headlands_and_bays" title="Headlands and bays">
        cape or headland
       </a>
       on a
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_mare" title="Lunar mare">
        mare
       </a>
       .
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terra">
        Terra
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_lunar_features&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Terra">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The continental areas between the seas were given comparable names by
       <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Riccioli" title="Giovanni Battista Riccioli">
        Giovanni Battista Riccioli
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but were opposite the names used for the seas. Thus there were the lands of sterility (Terra Sterilitatis), heat (Terra Caloris), and liveliness (Terra Vitae). However these names for the highland regions are no longer used on recent maps, and
       <i>
        Terrae
       </i>
       are not officially recognized as standard lunar nomenclature by the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union" title="International Astronomical Union">
        International Astronomical Union
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Name
        </th>
        <th>
         Name Origin
        </th>
        <th>
         Near side position
        </th>
       </tr>

        <td>

         Land of Cheerfulness
        </td>
        <td>
         Region southeast of
         <a href="/wiki/Mare_Crisium" title="Mare Crisium">
          Mare Crisium
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lpod_10-9">
          <a href="#cite_note-lpod-10">
           [10]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Terra Vitæ
        </td>
        <td>
         Land of Liveliness
        </td>
        <td>
         Northeast rim of the near side.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lpod_10-10">
          <a href="#cite_note-lpod-10">
           [10]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Craters">
        Craters
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_lunar_features&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Craters">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The large majority of these features are
       <a href="/wiki/Impact_crater" title="Impact crater">
        impact craters
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_nomenclature" title="Planetary nomenclature">
        crater nomenclature
       </a>
       is governed by the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union" title="International Astronomical Union">
        International Astronomical Union
       </a>
       , and this listing only includes features that are officially recognized by that scientific society.
      </p>
      <p>
       The lunar craters are listed in the following subsections. Where a formation has associated
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/satellite" title="wikt:satellite">
        satellite
       </a>
       craters, these are detailed on the main crater description pages.
      </p>
      <table border="1" cellpadding="4" cellspacing="0" style="text-align:center;margin: 0.5em 0 0.5em 0; background: #f9f9f9; border: 1px #aaa solid; border-collapse: collapse; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="6" style="background-color:#DDDDDD;">
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_craters_on_the_Moon" title="List of craters on the Moon">
          List of craters on the Moon
         </a>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Restoring+bright+names&amp;rft.pub=LPOD&amp;rft.date=2006-07-13&amp;rft.aulast=Wood&amp;rft.aufirst=Chuck&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.lpod.org%2F%3Fm%3D20060418&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+lunar+features">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
       </ol>
      </div>
      <p>
       These were used for references in the Water Features section.

       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20111218085633/http://www.lpi.usra.edu/resources/lunar_atlases/" rel="nofollow">
         Lunar Atlases
        </a>
        at the Lunar &amp; Planetary Institute
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.lpi.usra.edu/research/lunar_orbiter/" rel="nofollow">
           Digital Lunar Orbiter Photographic Atlas of the Moon
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.planet4589.org/astro/lunar" rel="nofollow">
         Lunar Nomenclature
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="http://LPOD.wikispaces.com" rel="nofollow">
         Lunar Photo of the Day
        </a>
        by Charles A. Wood
        <i>
         et al.
        </i>
       </li>
      </ul>
